  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e118bfc5-5304-40a3-9c4a-014f1fa30c1f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer10901351695570388812">#1 <em>New York Times</em> bestseller Maria Dahvana Headley’s soaring sky fantasy <em>Magonia</em> is now in paperback!<br/><br/>Since she was a baby, Aza Ray Boyle has suffered from a mysterious lung disease that makes it ever harder for her to breathe, to speak—to live. So when Aza catches a glimpse of a ship in the sky, her family chalks it up to a cruel side effect of her medication. But Aza does</span>
  <span id="freeText10901351695570388812" style="display:none">#1 <em>New York Times</em> bestseller Maria Dahvana Headley’s soaring sky fantasy <em>Magonia</em> is now in paperback!<br /><br />Since she was a baby, Aza Ray Boyle has suffered from a mysterious lung disease that makes it ever harder for her to breathe, to speak—to live. So when Aza catches a glimpse of a ship in the sky, her family chalks it up to a cruel side effect of her medication. But Aza doesn’t think this is a hallucination. She can hear someone on the ship calling her name.<br /><br />Only her best friend, Jason, listens. Jason, who’s always been there. Jason, for whom she might have more-than-friendly feelings. But before Aza can consider that thrilling idea, something goes terribly wrong. Aza is lost to our world—and found by another. Magonia.<br /><br />Above the clouds, in a land of trading ships, Aza is not the weak and dying thing she was. In Magonia, she can breathe for the first time. Better, she has immense power—but as she navigates her new life, she discovers that war between Magonia and Earth is coming. In Aza’s hands lies the fate of the whole of humanity—including the boy who loves her. Where do her loyalties lie?</span>
  <a data-text-id="10901351695570388812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

John Green use a melodramatic style like soap opera. Lots of tears and feelings, Death and live, repetitions ("...makes it ever harder for her to breathe, to speak—to live"). <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1099082408" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1099082408" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1099082408?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1099082408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13470828116081599705"><b>
  <i>I'm dark matter. The universe inside of me is full of something, and science can't even shine a light on it. I feel like I'm mostly made of mysteries.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Oh my... <i>Magonia</i> is one hell of a rare novel.<br/><br/>Not only does it offer an intriguing blend of reality-infused science fiction and highly-imaginative fantasy, but it is also <u>unlike anything I have ever read before.</u><br/><br/>I've always said that - for me - originality is one of the best and rarest compliments a writer can get. Not "this is the next <i>Hunger Ga</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13470828116081599705" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>I'm dark matter. The universe inside of me is full of something, and science can't even shine a light on it. I feel like I'm mostly made of mysteries.</i>
</b><br /><br />Oh my... <i>Magonia</i> is one hell of a rare novel.<br /><br />Not only does it offer an intriguing blend of reality-infused science fiction and highly-imaginative fantasy, but it is also <u>unlike anything I have ever read before.</u><br /><br />I've always said that - for me - originality is one of the best and rarest compliments a writer can get. Not "this is the next <i>Hunger Games</i> or <i>Harry Potter</i>" but "this is completely different to everything else I've read". How unusual it is to read a novel and be taken to places so new, fresh and wonderfully magical.<br /><br />One of my favourite things has always been when authors manage to weave fact and fiction together in order to create a fantasy story with added realism. Especially when they introduce me to parts of history I'd never heard about before. Did you know that in France in 815, sailors claimed to have come from a secret realm in the clouds they called Magonia? This was one of the first recorded instances of UFO-related occurrences and it was completely new to me.<br /><br />Many times I have wondered why YA authors insist on using the same old recycled mythology when there's a whole universe of weird and wonderful shit out there just begging to be turned into a story. Here we have a fine example. This book opens up an entire new world full of detailed and exciting mythology. I was like a kid in a toy store, staring wide-eyed at all the colourful weirdness and longing for more as the pages flew by.<br /><br />The author uses language that deserves the comparisons to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1221698.Neil_Gaiman" title="Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neil Gaiman</a> - a rich, atmospheric style of fairytale storytelling. And with this, she creates a cast of wonderful characters who I can only hope will reappear in sequels. <br /><br />The main character in <i>Magonia</i> is Aza Ray and she is dying. The doctors are unable to discover what is wrong with her and have failed at all attempts to cure her of the mysterious disease that is causing her to essentially drown in the Earth's atmosphere. Then one day, circumstances see Aza awakening in a whole new world where she is no longer weak and sickly, but a powerful creature at the centre of a longstanding feud that will take her to places she never could have dreamed existed.<br /><br />Suddenly, she discovers the truth about her life, her past and who she is; maybe this new world can offer her a place to live the kind of life she's always wanted? Or maybe nothing is as it seems. Stir in plenty of action, romance, and well-developed family dynamics and you have something pretty damn amazing. I should also point out that the love triangle I had feared might occur never went in that direction.<br /><br /><b>Looking for a genre-defying blend of magic, love, flying and family?</b> <br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13470828116081599705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1218303656" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1218303656" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1218303656?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=uncommon">uncommon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fast-paced">fast-paced</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1218303656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12867597245471485539"><strong>
  <em>I know everyone has dreams of flying, but this isn’t a dream of flying. It’s a dream of floating, and the ocean is not water but wind.</em>
</strong><br/><br/><strong>
  <em>I call it a dream, but it feels realer than my life.</em>
</strong><br/><br/>Breathe, Lola, breathe!<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425499753ra/13898631.gif' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Oh god. What did you do to me, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21393526.Magonia__Magonia___1_' title='Magonia (Magonia, #1) by Maria Dahvana Headley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Magonia</a>? How dare play with my emotions… over and over again? You showed me your careless, beautiful, powerful, pitiless and heart-wrenching sides… when I was not prepared for them. Is this how Aza felt, daily, living on Earth, her lungs not being abl</span>
  <span id="freeText12867597245471485539" style="display:none"><strong>
  <em>I know everyone has dreams of flying, but this isn’t a dream of flying. It’s a dream of floating, and the ocean is not water but wind.</em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>I call it a dream, but it feels realer than my life.</em>
</strong><br><br>Breathe, Lola, breathe!<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425499753ra/13898631.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh god. What did you do to me, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21393526.Magonia__Magonia___1_" title="Magonia (Magonia, #1) by Maria Dahvana Headley" rel="nofollow noopener">Magonia</a>? How dare play with my emotions… over and over again? You showed me your careless, beautiful, powerful, pitiless and heart-wrenching sides… when I was not prepared for them. Is this how Aza felt, daily, living on Earth, her lungs not being able to function properly? Well, if that was your goal, you <strong>succeeded</strong>.<br><br>Aza can’t breathe. Her disease is a mystery to every doctor and… incurable. She’s going to die soon; she always knew it would happen. Things are getting worst though. It’s when all her hopes falter and she feels herself weaken to a very dangerously sensitive and raw state that she sees something spectacular amid the sky: ships that sail into the air! What is the significance of this? Why is she the only one able to witness such thing? Is that…<br>Magonia?<br><br>While, by moment, it reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18166936.The_Strange_and_Beautiful_Sorrows_of_Ava_Lavender" title="The Strange and Beautiful Sorrows of Ava Lavender by Leslye Walton" rel="nofollow noopener">The Strange and Beautiful Sorrows of Ava Lavender</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8490112.Daughter_of_Smoke___Bone__Daughter_of_Smoke___Bone___1_" title="Daughter of Smoke &amp; Bone (Daughter of Smoke &amp; Bone, #1) by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Daughter of Smoke &amp; Bone</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21393526.Magonia__Magonia___1_" title="Magonia (Magonia, #1) by Maria Dahvana Headley" rel="nofollow noopener">Magonia</a> remains one of the most creative and original and unique stories I’ve read in years. I can’t even categorize it... it both felt like a magical realism story and a fantasy one. It was the kind of book that makes you believe in everything that is happening inside it and brings all of your senses to life, but it nonetheless did contain creatures of multiple sorts and an invisible-to-the-human-eye world surrounded by air.<br><br>Aza started off as impertinent and know-it-all and judgemental, but her peculiar and sarcastic humor charmed me:<strong>
  <em> Rare, like my disease is standing onstage in a tuxedo belting out a torch song that has a chorus along the lines of ‘‘Baby, you’re the only one for me.’’ And then the disease just stands there, waiting for me to walk into its arms and give up resisting.</em>
</strong> Who talks like that? No one. Loved it.<br><br>The great thing about Aza, you have to know, is that she experienced so much… and it changed her throughout the story. Her character development will <u>not</u> go unnoticed. I’m saying this because, if Aza gets on your nerves at the beginning, you might think about giving her another chance… She will prove you that she is more than she appears to be.<br><br>There was a love-triangle. But an interesting one. And it actually ‘‘made sense.’’ After all, Aza thought she would never ever see boy #1 and her and boy #2 had a rare bond that couldn’t be broken in a snap of finger.<br><br><strong>The writing… I devoured it.</strong> It had everything I consistently look forward to inside a writing style: figures of speech, short <em>and</em> long sentences, germane descriptions. And it also gave an appropriate depending-on-the-scene atmosphere to the story, which is something I think to be very salient when it comes to a narrative.<br><br><strong><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21393526.Magonia__Magonia___1_" title="Magonia (Magonia, #1) by Maria Dahvana Headley" rel="nofollow noopener">Magonia</a> is my favorite 2015 publication so far. Therefore, I am recommending it to you, reader.</strong></span>
  <a data-text-id="12867597245471485539" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1345334888" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1345334888" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1345334888?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=books-everyone-loves-but-me">books-everyone-loves-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=oh-no-biiiiiiirds">oh-no-biiiiiiirds</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1345334888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2367507257472399500">looks like i am the only one who didn't fall head-over-heels in love with this book. i <i>did</i> fall pretty hard for the cover, but it takes more than a pretty face to win me over…<br/><br/>it has many good qualities: story set in a wholly original fantasy world, families who are supportive and loving that seem realistic rather than idealized, strong imagery and situations that aren't just warmed-over versions of other YA books, romance where the two participants are apart for most of the book, so we don't hav</span>
  <span id="freeText2367507257472399500" style="display:none">looks like i am the only one who didn't fall head-over-heels in love with this book. i <i>did</i> fall pretty hard for the cover, but it takes more than a pretty face to win me over…<br><br>it has many good qualities: story set in a wholly original fantasy world, families who are supportive and loving that seem realistic rather than idealized, strong imagery and situations that aren't just warmed-over versions of other YA books, romance where the two participants are apart for most of the book, so we don't have to read about all the gazing and fumbling and stammering, debilitating illness written sympathetically and vividly... <br><br>i just didn't think the actual story was developed as well as the characters. i never felt the tension i was meant to feel during the actiony events, and beyond the two main characters: aza and jason, none of the other characters were more than foils or obstacles, and overall the fantasy elements were not as well-realized as the realistic ones. <br><br>aza has been severely sick her whole life with a respiratory condition so rare that it has actually been named after her, and whose cause and treatment has baffled every last specialist. she is nearly sixteen, much older than she was ever expected to live, when she begins seeing visions of ships in the clouds and hearing something whistling and calling her name. assuming these are hallucinations brought on by one of her medications, she freaks out less than she might ordinarily, until the evening she is visited by an assortment of BIRDS (if you know how i feel about birds, you know how alarming this is), after which she collapses and dies in the ambulance on the way to the hospital. <br><br>when she wakes up, she is aboard the very ship she has been "hallucinating," high in the air, where she is re-introduced to her people, because - turns out, she's not from "our" world, she is from magonia, and it's the air on the earth that has been killing her. and there's no specialist for <i>that</i>. <br><br>so aza learns about her culture and their rituals, and the BIRD that belongs in HER CHEST and that she is a very special girl with a very special destiny. because YA. however, she has left behind her parents and sister, as well as her best friend-with-possibilities, jason, and even though they all think she's dead, and she has finally found a place where she can breathe, she's torn between two worlds.<br><br>and jason, for one, doesn't believe she's really dead.<br><br>this one got off to a rocky start for me, because from the outset, i was not a fan of aza's voice. i think she was meant to come off as tough in the face of death or something, but her brittle snark was irritating. her illness was horrible, and i'm not downplaying her struggle, but i also don't automatically canonize the afflicted and i think that when people are bitchy and then say things like <i>"Calling the sick girl names? Please. We all know it's not okay"</i> - it's not fair. if you're going to antagonize people and be provocative, you're gonna get some back, sick or not - no special treatment in high school politics. <br><br>but after a while, i got into it, and once jason was introduced, it got a bit better. although it's still "what if john green kids were even <i>more</i> precocious," and they don't read like sixteen-year-olds, it's still a really lovely relationship, and i thought headley did a nice job turning that friendship into maybe-more without it getting all goopy. despite sounding older and being more capable than their years (booking flights, tossing off profitable inventions and having factories in their arsenal, having access to seeecret footage of squids, etc..) i thought the bones of their friendship rang true - nerdy social outcasts finding each other and bonding over pi and the OED. it's very sweet and charming. <br><br>i also loved the descriptions of some of the creatures in magonia. not the heartbirds (shudder) or bird-people (bigger shudder), but batsails, squallwhales, stormsharks?? yes pretty please! <i>Can anything I will ever hear from now until the end of time sound cooler than stormsharks?</i> probably not. but that's the thing - a lot of the magonia stuff was just window dressing without a lot of depth. we don't even get to spend any time with stormsharks, they are just a passing detail. <br><br>the strengths of this book are completely terrestrial - aza's family, jason's family, and their unshakeable friendship. the fantasy is blurry, the avatar-level eco-preach unnuanced, and the story a little flimsy. i'll read the second one, in the hopes that book two will have way more stormsharks, but i didn't swoon over this one the way it seems the rest of the world did. <br><br>mea culpa.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2367507257472399500" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1273115194" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1273115194" />
    <a title="Chantal " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31668723-chantal"><img alt="Chantal " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464626501p2/31668723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1273115194?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chantal " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chantal " href="/user/show/31668723-chantal">Chantal </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=published-2015">published-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=listened-on-audio">listened-on-audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1273115194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4990036533368463166"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Before I start my review can we just all take a moment to appreciate this GORGEOUS cover? Yes? Yes.<br/><br/>Throughout this entire story I kept seeing certain images in my mind. Something like this<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433753435ra/15138062.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>and this<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433754436ra/15138174.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I can’t have been the only one, right? I mean, <b>cities in the sky, flying ships, air pirates, strange creatures in the clouds</b>… Having said that though, this comparison is a compliment, not a reproach. <b>By no means did I feel like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21393526.Magonia__Magonia___1_' title='Magonia (Magonia, #1) by Maria Dahvana Headley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Magonia</a> was a copy of <i>Castle in the Sky</i>. Rather, me comparing a boo</b></span>
  <span id="freeText4990036533368463166" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br><br>Before I start my review can we just all take a moment to appreciate this GORGEOUS cover? Yes? Yes.<br><br>Throughout this entire story I kept seeing certain images in my mind. Something like this<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433753435ra/15138062.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and this<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433754436ra/15138174.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can’t have been the only one, right? I mean, <b>cities in the sky, flying ships, air pirates, strange creatures in the clouds</b>… Having said that though, this comparison is a compliment, not a reproach. <b>By no means did I feel like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21393526.Magonia__Magonia___1_" title="Magonia (Magonia, #1) by Maria Dahvana Headley" rel="nofollow noopener">Magonia</a> was a copy of <i>Castle in the Sky</i>. Rather, me comparing a book to a Myazaki movie is pretty much the biggest praise I can give.</b> <br><br>So what is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21393526.Magonia__Magonia___1_" title="Magonia (Magonia, #1) by Maria Dahvana Headley" rel="nofollow noopener">Magonia</a> actually about? <br><br>It’s the story of Aza Ray, a fifteen-year-old girl that has been suffering from a strange and foreign disease her entire life. She has trouble breathing and basically feels like she’s drowning in air. She is dying and all attempts to cure her have failed. Then one day, Aza sees a ship in the sky and at around the same time the doctors discover a feather in her lungs. She finds out that she isn’t wholly part of the human world but belongs to a different place, a place in the clouds. I’ll let you discover the rest.<br><br><b><i>Magonia</i> stood out to me because of its originality and imagination.</b> Despite the fact, that the plot arch at its very core is your typical YA fantasy story (girl is weak, finds out she isn’t what she thought but that she is in actuality “special” blablabla), <i>Magonia</i> is still unlike anything I’ve ever read before. And originality, for me, is one of the most important factors in my enjoyment of a book. The <b>ideas in this book were new and fresh, the mythology unheard of</b>. I loved that about the novel.<br><br>Having said that though, this <b>novel didn’t blow me away</b>. In fact, it didn’t even come close, which is really sad considering its potential. <b>My problem here was in the execution of the story.</b> <br><br>Basically, the <b>plot felt very haphazard</b>. A lot of the time <b>I felt confused</b> because I wasn’t sure what was happening. I actually found myself having to reread pages because I realized that I had missed something important and was totally lost. This usually never happens to me with books I read for personal enjoyment. <b>The plotline really needed that extra polish and fleshing out that would have made the story better understandable and less exhausting to read. The conflict felt weakly grounded and there was too much happening at the same time</b>, so that none of the elements could be executed with care. <br><br>The <b>world building</b> definitely also contributed to my general confusion. Although I had the feeling that the author had a solid idea for the world in her head with lots of enticing ideas, she didn’t manage to translate that onto the page. As a result, she would just drop an “information bomb” on us, e.g. in the form of a magical creature, but then wouldn’t explain anything about said creature. <b>I would often find myself wondering what the purpose of a certain story element was, where things had come from, how the world worked. We got almost zero historical, cultural or political background of this world above our human one.</b> <br><br>All in all, this <b>book just lacked much needed explanation</b>. It’s great if you can give me something unique and charming, but if there isn’t enough information or explanation I’m not going believe it and I’m going to go through the novel constantly unsure of whether or not I missed something.<br><br>I quite enjoyed the characters. <b>Aza was smart and sarcastic with a very peculiar sense of humor</b> and I liked her well enough. I did however, have an issue with the <b>inconstancy of her character</b>. She constantly <b>switched sides and trusted the wrong people for no apparent reason</b>. She seemed to understand things and make accurate judgments but then didn’t act on them. I had trouble understanding her motivation for some of her actions, which caused me to feel detached from her.<br><br><b>Jason</b> was more consistent but I didn’t really connect with him either. I liked him as a character, he was a <b>nice guy, but I couldn’t love him</b>. Also, how on earth he managed certain things <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[seriously, a sixteen-year-old boy manages to smuggle himself into a high-security seed repository halfway across the world? Just how? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> will remain a mystery to me. <br><br>The <b>romance aspect in this novel was solid</b>. There was no insta-love or ungrounded angst. I actually understood why the two characters were in love with each other, which I appreciate. However, it also wasn’t the kind of romance that blew me away and made me skip up and down. <br><br>The <b>writing is definitely a hit or miss</b>. The narrative style is quite different from what I usually read, <b>very conversational and sarcastic</b>. Personally, I enjoyed it after I got into it but it wasn’t my favorite. Here a quote that I think captures the writing style quite well:<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Did he just say stormsharks? My inner nerd is elated. Can anything I will ever hear from now until the end of time sound cooler than stormsharks?</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br>Overall, an enjoyable read but I wouldn’t recommend it to everyone. It really depends on how you feel about the writing style and how important worldbuilding is to you. <br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4990036533368463166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1085542534" />
    <a title="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5478965-aimee-aimee-always"><img alt="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562987681p2/5478965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" href="/user/show/5478965-aimee-aimee-always">Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=covergasm">covergasm</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=might-make-you-shit-bricks">might-make-you-shit-bricks</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1085542534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14946798524339168307">More reviews like this one on <a href='http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Social Potato</a>.<br/><br/>If you're going to ask me to describe <em>Magonia</em> in one word, that word would be <em>charming</em>. <strong>It was elegant, magical and absolutely captivating</strong>.<br/><br/>Reading this book was like floating on a magical, puffy, pink cloud. While eating fairy dust and watching shooting stars. <em>That's</em> how alluring this book was. The only other time I've felt this way was while watching the <em>Stardust</em> movie!<br/><br/>While Aza wasn't physically strong, <strong>personality-wise, she was feisty and sassy</strong>,</span>
  <span id="freeText14946798524339168307" style="display:none">More reviews like this one on <a href="http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net" rel="nofollow noopener">The Social Potato</a>.<br /><br />If you're going to ask me to describe <em>Magonia</em> in one word, that word would be <em>charming</em>. <strong>It was elegant, magical and absolutely captivating</strong>.<br /><br />Reading this book was like floating on a magical, puffy, pink cloud. While eating fairy dust and watching shooting stars. <em>That's</em> how alluring this book was. The only other time I've felt this way was while watching the <em>Stardust</em> movie!<br /><br />While Aza wasn't physically strong, <strong>personality-wise, she was feisty and sassy</strong>, which is why it was no wonder I was immediately entertained by her narrative. I felt like I casually slipped into Aza's mind while reading, and <strong>her perspective's such an interesting one</strong>, considering her unique condition and odd personality.<br /><br /><strong>She also had such an amazing relationship with her best friend <s>and the love of my life</s>, Jason</strong>. It's amazing how they're both quirky, and they just have this natural closeness that makes you want to push their faces together while screaming, <em>"Just kiss already!"</em> <strong>Jason was such a sweetheart, and it was absolutely heartwarming to see that he was willing to go through such lengths to get his best friend back</strong>.<br /><br />There is a sort-of-but-not-really love triangle, but I can't really go into detail without spoiling. Let's just say that romance lovers need not worry--the other half of the triangle made sense, and the everything went down smoothly.<br /><br />While the characters and their relationships were fabulous, I can honestly say that the best part about this novel was the world-building. This book is based off a more unknown mythology, and let me just say that <strong><em>Magonia</em> has one of the most gorgeous settings I have ever had the honor of reading about</strong>. Everything was so imaginative and vivid, with talking birds, singing birds, and a flying ship in the sky. Sounds crazy? Maybe. But it's the good kind of crazy. <strong>It's... wondrously strange.</strong><br /><br />And OH GOD, the writing, you guys. You know how much I'm not a fan of the more lyrical prose, but <strong>Headley's writing just made the story much more <em>real</em></strong>. Like floating on a magical pink cloud, indeed. It was just so elegant yet simple and easy to get into. <strong>Feeling what Aza and Jason felt was just natural with this glorious writing</strong>. (Not kidding--I may have cried a few times.) I fell in love with it from page one!<br /><br />The gist of it is that THIS BOOK IS AMAZING AND YOU SHOULD ALL BUY IT AND READ IT <s>AND PET IT</s>. Yep. That sounds about right.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14946798524339168307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1218468348" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1218468348" />
    <a title="destini mia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13742215-destini-mia"><img alt="destini mia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499903277p2/13742215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1218468348?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destini mia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destini mia" href="/user/show/13742215-destini-mia">destini mia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13742215-destini-mia?shelf=the-holy-grail">the-holy-grail</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1218468348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14226076945954946060"><blockquote>
<i>Aza,</i> it says, the whistle. <i>Aza, are you out there?</i>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436286831ra/15442592.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>It's been a really long time since I've read something so unique.</b> The premise, characters, setting . . . everything was just so <i>refreshing</i>. <br/><i>
  <blockquote>Aza Ray, your life is so gigantically not what you thought it was going to be. </blockquote>
</i><br/>I was warned that <i>Magonia</i> might be a little weird but, strangely, I didn't find it so. Maybe because I was forewarned . . . or maybe I'm the weird one and felt right at home reading <i>Magonia</i>. <br/><i>
  <blockquote>I'm something else. Something i</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText14226076945954946060" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<i>Aza,</i> it says, the whistle. <i>Aza, are you out there?</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436286831ra/15442592.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>It's been a really long time since I've read something so unique.</b> The premise, characters, setting . . . everything was just so <i>refreshing</i>. <br><i>
  <blockquote>Aza Ray, your life is so gigantically not what you thought it was going to be. </blockquote>
</i><br>I was warned that <i>Magonia</i> might be a little weird but, strangely, I didn't find it so. Maybe because I was forewarned . . . or maybe I'm the weird one and felt right at home reading <i>Magonia</i>. <br><i>
  <blockquote>I'm something else. Something important. What? No cue.</blockquote>
</i><br>Aza's character was one that may not be likable to everyone, but had me giggling at every turn. Was she kind of bitchy? Yes. But what can I say? I guess that's my kind of character. <br><i>
  <blockquote>Bang, bang, you're dead. Close your eyes and go to bed.</blockquote>
</i><br>She's suffered from a mystery lung/breathing condition that has left her on Death's doorstep most of her life.<br><i>
  <blockquote>My thing is a Mystery and not just a Mystery, but Bermuda– no sun, only Triangle. <br>Unknowable. Unsolvable. <br>I take handfuls of drugs every morning, even though no one is entirely sure what the thing that's wrong with me actually is. I'm rare like that.</blockquote>
</i><br>But she's destined for more than that. Magonia. A place where ships fly in the sky and the air is breathable. A place where she's not the weak, frail girl she's been most of her life. In <i>Magonia</i>, she's incredibly powerful. <br><i>
  <blockquote>Like I'm in a movie,<br>like I'm not me, <br>like I'm someone I never imagined<br>–bigger, stronger, and fearless. </blockquote>
</i><br>Jason, how did I grow attached to you so quickly?<br><i>
  <blockquote>He merely looks at you, blankly and conquers.</blockquote>
</i><br>I can't resist a guy that bends over backwards for the ones he loves. I got to hand it to him, he's much more open-minded than I am. He unwaveringly believed in Aza, no matter how certifiably insane the situation sounded. Honestly, I think everybody should have a Jason. <br><i>
  <blockquote>If she were here, listening to me, she'd be puking right now because I'm losing all my dignity.</blockquote>
</i><br>Jason + Aza<br>I ship it so hard. <b>
  <i>So hard.</i>
</b><br><br>The writing was unconventional but fit the story and characters perfectly. The author grabs your attention immediately and leaves you wanting so much more once you've finished. If I had started <i>Magonia</i> at night, it's easily a book I could have pulled an all-nighter with (and with little regret the next morning). That right there is 5 star worthy. <br><br>Along with the fact that, <b>not even 30% in, this book had me in tears</b>. <br><i>
  <blockquote>I know everyone has dreams of flying, but this isn't a dream of flying. It's a dream of floating, and the ocean is not water but wind.<br>I call the it a dream, but it feels realer than my life.</blockquote>
</i><br>What I especially loved about this story is how original it was. I could count on one hand, hell one finger, how many books I've read about a world in the sky like this one. I wasn't reading about the same old, overused concepts. This here was completely new mythology to me and <b>I ate it up</b> like cake. There was perfect mix of realism and fantasy in <i>Magonia</i>. It makes it feel <b>real</b> and not like fantasy. Like I could look out my window and into the sky and see an army of ships in the distance. <br><br>My only complaint is that there was a relationship bordering on a love triangle. But even that couldn't stop me from loving this book. I'm just slightly concerned on how that will play out in the sequel, but for now, I'm going to do what I do best and enjoy this uncomplicated, blissful relationship and ignore any kind of heinous love triangle that may come my way. <br><i>
  <blockquote>This isn't just Jason and Aza. It's not me racing against death to save her anymore. It's us racing against the impossible. </blockquote>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436305760i/15444976.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">.<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436305760i/15444977.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436305760i/15444978.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">.<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436305760i/15444979.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436311441i/15445735.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">.<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436311441i/15445736.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14226076945954946060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1108178105" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1108178105" />
    <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata"><img alt="Faye, la Patata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557835753p2/7650833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1108178105?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=subtle-but-giddy-worthy-romance">subtle-but-giddy-worthy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=adorable-love-interest">adorable-love-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=heart-doing-blackflips">heart-doing-blackflips</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=multiple-povs">multiple-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=finding-oneself">finding-oneself</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1108178105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17222083508784873648"><strong>First off, this was such a beautiful novel, inside and out.</strong><br/><blockquote>
  <i>I like the sky. It's rational to me in a way that life isn't. Looking at it doesn't suck the way you might think it would, given all the dying-girl-stares-at-heaven possibilities. I don't think of the sky as any kind of heaven item. I think of it as a bunch of gases and faraway echoes of things that used to be on fire.</i>
</blockquote><br/>When I read the first few paragraphs of this book, I initially thought it was the diary of a self-absorbed girl who t</span>
  <span id="freeText17222083508784873648" style="display:none"><strong>First off, this was such a beautiful novel, inside and out.</strong><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I like the sky. It's rational to me in a way that life isn't. Looking at it doesn't suck the way you might think it would, given all the dying-girl-stares-at-heaven possibilities. I don't think of the sky as any kind of heaven item. I think of it as a bunch of gases and faraway echoes of things that used to be on fire.</i>
</blockquote><br />When I read the first few paragraphs of this book, I initially thought it was the diary of a self-absorbed girl who thought she was the shit. <strong>After finishing the first two chapters, I ate my words and realized that the heroine was actually exploding with a certain kind of wisdom only a mature person who accepted her upcoming death could achieve.</strong><br /><blockquote>
  <em>Speaking of ocean and big fish in it. This is the first footage of a giant squid ever taken in which the squid is swimming around in its own environment. Imagine this sea-monstery unbelievable thing with eyeballs the size of a person's head, and a body and tentacles twenty-five feet long. As long as a school bus. Now, realize that no one's ever seen one moving around down there before. It's a pretty huge miracle, and if this exists, maybe there are things in Loch Ness, too. Maybe there are things everywhere, all over the place. Maybe there is... hope?</em>
  <br />
  <br />
  <em>Because every time someone finds a new animal, or a new amazing thing on earth, it means we haven't broken everything yet.</em>
</blockquote><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1099082408?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Emily May, in her review, likened the writing to Neil Gaiman's</a>, and she's very accurate with her assessment. Aza Ray was a dying girl, and she knew it. She talked about how her life has been since she was diagnosed with a breathing problem, and how she adjusted and her family adjusted to make her feel better and more comfortable. She would even make fun of herself sometimes, giving the narration self-deprecating moments that just make her even more endearing. You can actually <em>feel</em> how weak she was, and how it was her family and friend who were giving her strength to endure it all.  <strong>With such a situation, you'd think the atmosphere would be filled with drama, but the narration was just brimming with an uncommon honesty, full of raw emotions and hope and a sense of defeat, while also effortlessly making the mood somehow surreal at the same time. And funny. Don't forget funny.</strong><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I, myself, have never gotten my period, which I'm actually not too upset about. Postpone the misery, I say. It's because I'm too skinny, and have no luck gaining weight.</i>
  <br />
  <br />
  <em>Clarification: by "too skinny," I don't mean Sexy Goth Girl in Need of Flowery Dress and Lipstick to Become Girl Who Was Always Secretly Pretty but We Never Saw It till Now. I mean: dead girl walking. Corpse-style skin, and sometimes when I cough, it's way gross. Just saying.</em>
</blockquote><br />Or this:<br /><blockquote>
  <em>When Jason feels inclined, he's been known to make chocolate éclairs. Today he feels inclined. If I weren't already worried, this'd worry me. Chocolate éclairs are for birthdays. If he's making them early, I must really look bad.</em>
  <br />
  <br />
  <em>Yeah. I think I'll avoid the mirror.</em>
</blockquote><br /><strong> But wow, when the scene's emotional, it really hits you.</strong> There was this scene that lasted a good 10% of the book, and I cried all the way. I know I'm a crybaby, but when you saw <strong>how</strong> I was crying and <strong>how</strong> my heart was being pulled at different places, you just realize how powerful the book and the author are, impacting you so much when we barely even knew the heroine yet.<br /><blockquote>
  <em>My dad is fading out. All I can see are my own eyelashes and my eye own eyelids, and somehow, also, my own brain, all the pathways inside it, everything dark and narrow, and getting narrower, bookshelves closing in, books crushed, falling into muddled piles, pages crushed, words mangled, and me, running through it all, trying to get out before the walls collapse.</em>
  <br />
  <br />
  <em>I feel the entire inside of my body folding up, some kind of awful origami. I thought it would hurt, but the pain I've been feeling forever and ever is actually something that's ceasing to matter to me, just like my bones no longer matter to me, and I inhale, and exhale, and</em>
  <br />
  <br />
  <em>Bird in my chest</em>
  <br />
  <br />
  <em>Bird in my chest</em>
  <br />
  <br />
  <em>Bird in my chest</em>
  <br />
  <br />
  <em>Ships in the sky</em>
  <br />
  <br />
  <em>Last moments before dying</em>
</blockquote><br /><strong>The rest of the novel was equally fascinating. The plot here, while not be one hundred original (girl finding out who she really is, comes to possess mysterious and unimaginable powers), still feels refreshing because of the world-building that's absolutely and entirely new (at least to me it felt like it). </strong>Instead of borrowing from overused mythologies that we're already so familiar with, we're introduced to something that came from a French medieval tale, and man, was it an adventure riding the skies with them Magonian creatures. <strong>I always rejoice when we're treated to new concepts because it also meant broadening your knowledge of the world's tales, many of them long forgotten, itching to be told and presented to the world again in a modern way.</strong><br /><br />And Maria Dehvana Headley did it right with this book.<br /><br /><strong>The other characters were such a delight, too. Jason Kerwin might just be the most adorable guy ever.</strong> He's Aza's best friend, fascinated with computers and numbers and the world, someone I could just fricking relate to,  and doesn't say anything so sugary, or flirt so openly. He's just being himself and uses small gestures to communicate his feelings and it's so bloody heartwarming. The family dynamics were so awesome, too. You can just see how much family plays a huge role in Aza's life, her family's kindness influencing her and reminding her of what's important. They're not absent at all<strong>. They were present even when they weren't there, because early on, you already witness how big of a mark they put in her life.</strong><br /><br />Overall, this was a beautiful book, and not just because of the cover. The writing is charming and bewitching at the same time. The pages are full of honesty, love, fun, friendship, and magic, and will surely introduce you to places and heights you've never been to before. Get ready to be surprised this upcoming April!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17222083508784873648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1297793171" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1297793171" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1297793171?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062391674" href="/book/show/23215491-magonia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1297793171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3681372307208938766"><b>"There was no way I could live another moment without Aza Ray knowing my name."</b><br/><br/>I was first drawn to this book because of the description that many, many people made of it. They usually used an adjective, one magic word which alone can move, create and destroy universes: <b>'gaimanian'</b>. They said this book was like this: gaimanian. <br/>Well.<br/>Let's analyse this word.<br/><br/>gaiman = that Gaiman? The freakin' fabulous author of masterpieces like <i>Stardust</i> and <i>American Gods</i>? <i>That</i> Gaiman? <br/>-ian = please take me I'm yo</span>
  <span id="freeText3681372307208938766" style="display:none"><b>"There was no way I could live another moment without Aza Ray knowing my name."</b><br /><br />I was first drawn to this book because of the description that many, many people made of it. They usually used an adjective, one magic word which alone can move, create and destroy universes: <b>'gaimanian'</b>. They said this book was like this: gaimanian. <br />Well.<br />Let's analyse this word.<br /><br />gaiman = that Gaiman? The freakin' fabulous author of masterpieces like <i>Stardust</i> and <i>American Gods</i>? <i>That</i> Gaiman? <br />-ian = please take me I'm yours let's have a lot of baby books together.<br /><br />So, yeah, I was pretty excited for <i>Magonia</i>. But, while some of my expectations were fully met, others weren't.<br /><br />It's a good book. It has a <b>compelling plot</b> and <b>interesting characters</b>. The <b>world-building</b> cannot be said to be uninteresting. The <b>writing</b> is beyond any doubt <b>peculiar</b> and <b>pleasant</b> to read.<br />But:<br /><br />• The <b> plot</b> presents <b>more than just one deadlock</b>, and <b>some things, in my opinion, didn't make much sense</b>. For one thing, why does Aza have to steal a boat in order to free a bird? Didn't it suffice to bring it outdoors and free it there? I know that Aza had to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[leave the ship so as to create an occasion for the Breath to kidnap her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but this is called forcing the plot, and honestly I can't help turning up my nose at it. <br />Also, Jason. It's as if this boy has a passe-partout to every door. The more reserved the information is, the easier he manages to get it. The results of an autopsy? He can have it. Hacking every computer in the USA? Child's play. False documents to get to Norway? No problem. False document for Aza to get her back home from Norway? Nothing ahs ever been easier.<br />I don't know why, but I'm under the impression that's not how things work in reality. Like, at all.<br /><br />• Speaking about the <b>characters</b>, the only one with whom I could completely connect is <b>Jason</b> (despite his inexplicable I-can-get-what-the-heck-I-want superpowers). His pages, the ones following <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Aza's supposed death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> made me weep buckets of tears, so deep, moving and honest his voice his. Those pages are my favourites in the whole book.<br /><b>Aza</b> is not as interesting as she seemed to be at the beginning and as she had the potential to be. She's not annoying or excessively conventional either, but I wouldn't include her in my top list of favourite heroines.<br /><b>Dai</b> really bothered me, because he has absolutely no characterizations. We are told his story through another character, and it's a very sad story, or, better, it's supposed to be. I didn't feel pity for him, nor sadness. For him, I didn't feel anything at all. He does not have a voice. He starts acting like an asshole, and then he begins being kind of tender towards Aza. That's where his characterization begins and where it ends.<br />The other characters did not impress me. Aza's and Jason's family are depicted in a particularly realistic way, which I appreciated a lot, but they have very few scene in the book. <b>Captain Zal</b> is a little too stereotypical for my own tastes, but I don't exclude she could gain in terms of characterization in the next instalment.<br /><br />• The <b>world-building</b>: was I the only one to feel like something was missing? I think that probably some more explanations were needed. I'm not one for info-dump, but if you can't provide all the necessary informations indirectly through the dialogues or so on, maybe you could indulge in some informative passages. For instance, I would have liked to know some things more about Magonia, by whom is it ruled, or how big it is and how can its system work if all that they have come from Earth, how they developed ships able to fly, why they and the Earthens didn't mingle from the beginning, why some Earthens end up living there... I don't know, something. Instead it's like, down there there is Earth, up there there is Magonia, that's all you need to know.<br />On the other hand, I loved, loved, <i>loved</i> the <b>lungbirds </b>thing. It's kind of <b>poetic</b>, isn't it? You personal bird who sing with you, only with you. Oh, and it dwells in your lung. That may be kind of unsettling, but to me it's still poetic. Yes, I am <i>that</i> morbid.<br /><br />• The <b>writing style</b> has its ups and downs. I was totally mesmerized by it in some passages, couldn't stand it in others. And I should say that I loathe the use of caps lock in novels and formal writing, so that's another thing that didn't work in favour oh Headley's style, at least for me. But generally speaking, it charmed me.<br /><br /><b>"If you look at the sky that way, it’s this massive shifting poem, or maybe a letter, first written by one author, and then, when the earth moves, annotated by another. So I stare and stare until, one day, I can read it."</b><br /><br />Long story short, despite the many things that didn't fully convinced me, <b>
  <i>Magonia</i>
</b> is still a <b>beautiful</b>,<b> unusual</b>, <b>whimsical</b> and <b>elegant</b> story that will put a spell on your heart. <br />If I'm going to read the sequel? Absolutely yes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3681372307208938766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1083486619" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413275441p2/10890208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1083486619?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=not-bad-at-all">not-bad-at-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=writing-envy">writing-envy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1083486619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15113418488992782451">See more reviews at <a href='http://yamidnightreads.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/>It's been 3.5 weeks since I've read <i>Magonia </i>and since then I have bought this book for 2 people, recommended it to all of my friends, given away a copy as a Twitter giveaway and broken my book buying ban (that only managed to last 3 days) to buy myself the hardcover of the book. So I guess it's safe to say that <strong>I really <em>really </em>like this book</strong>.<br/><br/>They weren't kidding when they said that Maria Dahvana Headley's writing is <strong>comparable to the works of <em>Neil Gaiman</em></strong>. Bec</span>
  <span id="freeText15113418488992782451" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br /><br />It's been 3.5 weeks since I've read <i>Magonia </i>and since then I have bought this book for 2 people, recommended it to all of my friends, given away a copy as a Twitter giveaway and broken my book buying ban (that only managed to last 3 days) to buy myself the hardcover of the book. So I guess it's safe to say that <strong>I really <em>really </em>like this book</strong>.<br /><br />They weren't kidding when they said that Maria Dahvana Headley's writing is <strong>comparable to the works of <em>Neil Gaiman</em></strong>. Because <em>Magonia</em>? <strong>This book had me eating up each and every word.</strong><br /><blockquote>If you look at the sky that way, it’s this massive shifting poem, or maybe a letter, first written by one author, and then, when the earth moves, annotated by another. So I stare and stare until, one day, I can read it.</blockquote><br /><em>Magnolia </em>is about Aza Ray who is slowly dying. What I feared most was for this book to be about a self-pitying girl who would sit in the corner and wallow away about how her life totally sucks. But thank God, this is not that story. No - this is the story about a girl with a peculiar lung disease who soon dies and awakes in a completely new world where she can not only breathe, but also finds herself in the middle of a feud between two worlds. And to top off <strong>a completely refreshing story line that plays a lot with mythological aspects</strong>, we get an incredibly entertaining main character. Aza Ray is <strong>sassy, smart and funny without really trying</strong>. She definitely has that dark humour thing going on and I absolutely loved that about her.<br /><blockquote>I myself have never gotten my period, which I'm actually not too upset about. Postpone the misery, I say. It's because I'm too skinny, and have no luck gaining weight.<br /><br />Clarification: by "too skinny," I don't mean Sexy Goth Girl in Need of Flowery Dress and Lipstick to Become Girl Who Was Always Secretly Pretty but We Never Saw It till Now. I mean: dead girl walking. Corpse-style skin, and sometimes when I cough, it's way gross. Just saying.</blockquote><br />I was very surprised to find out that this book is actually in <strong>told in dual POV</strong>. While at first I found it really irrelevant for Jason (Aza Ray's best friend and <em>possibly hopefully</em> something else by the end of the book) to have his own chapters, you soon see why it's so necessary for his voice to be present throughout, and I seriously loved it. Jason is one of those really nice and sweet guys who are just so darn reliable and authentic. <strong>He's undeniably cute and loved how he was always looking out for Aza,</strong> but isn't just stupidly and blindly 'in love' and has no life apart from Aza. The guy has a brain and knows how to use it.<br /><br />In general, I loved the world that Headley has introduced to us. <strong>It's ethereal, magical, and painfully spectacular.</strong> I loved the creation of a new Magonian race and the complexity and detail the Headley gave them. <strong>This author has an amazing imagination that I truly envy. </strong><br /><br /><strong><em>Magonia </em>is definitely not a book you want to be missing. It is certainly going down as one of my top 15 of 2015, and I'm sure it'll make many of your lists as well. Read. This. Book. </strong><br /><p>
  <em>~Thank you HarperCollins Australia for sending me this copy!~</em>
</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="15113418488992782451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText15815465422531322236" style="display:none">This book was confusing. <br /><br />I really enjoyed the first 100 pages or so, but as soon as "the thing" happens, it all sort of fell apart for me. Those first 100 pages were well paced, witty, fun - but then the story basically changes completely. It dragged, I had a hard time connecting with the new world and new characters, and I'm not sure it all came together for me by the end. <br /><br />It felt like the book didn't have enough time to become what it was trying to be in the second part, and while the middle dragged, the ending felt incredibly rushed. I zoomed through the beginning, excited about the story, and then struggled through the last 2/3.<br /><br />It was a weird book. Some may love it, but I don't think it was for me.</span>

<div id="review_1244411094" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon (It Starts At Midnight)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon (It Starts At Midnight)" href="/user/show/8652150-shannon-it-starts-at-midnight">Shannon (It Starts At Midnight)</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062320544" href="/book/show/22864466-magonia">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1244411094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16248912027448805930">Well, crap. Here I am again, black sheeping my way through a book that <em>everyone</em> and their mom seems to love. I think this is most likely a case of <strong>me</strong> being the problem as opposed to the book being the problem. I really just didn't get it.<br/><br/>There <em>were</em> good parts, don't get me wrong. There was even a time when I was really getting into it! Here's how it went down:<br/> 
  <strong>The Beginning</strong>
 <br/><p>So, Aza has some mystery illness that no doctor can figure out and that causes her to have breathing issues. That has t</p></span>
  <span id="freeText16248912027448805930" style="display:none">Well, crap. Here I am again, black sheeping my way through a book that <em>everyone</em> and their mom seems to love. I think this is most likely a case of <strong>me</strong> being the problem as opposed to the book being the problem. I really just didn't get it.<br /><br />There <em>were</em> good parts, don't get me wrong. There was even a time when I was really getting into it! Here's how it went down:<br /> 
  <strong>The Beginning</strong>
 <br /><p>So, Aza has some mystery illness that no doctor can figure out and that causes her to have breathing issues. That has to be very difficult. Also difficult is Aza's attitude. But her friend Jason was pretty great, so I stuck with it, even though I was a bit bored. Then I actually started to enjoy their friendship, and the "will they or won't they?" thing, and it started tugging on my feels. There were points that I was in tears over Aza and Jason and her sickness, and other spoilery stuff that I won't mention. Suffice it to say, I was really starting to enjoy the book.<br /><br /></p> 
  <strong>And Then....</strong>
 <br /><p><strong>Bird people.</strong> With giant ships in the sky. The hell?! I just.... couldn't. First of all, I was confused. So, so confused. What <em>are</em> bird people exactly? I was basically picturing a team mascot.<br /></p><p>Things in the beginning had moved slow, and then suddenly Aza is a bird person, in this whole new world, and I simply couldn't keep up. And also, it was kind of too weird and I stopped caring.<br /></p><p>There were a few things I enjoyed, though. The writing was very pretty, and Jason was fantastic as a character (even though some of the stuff about him was <em>highly</em> unrealistic, his character itself was great). And, some of the stuff at the end was pretty enjoyable, so there's that.<br /></p><p>But it seemed rushed in general. There was a <em>lot</em> of stuff crammed into 320 pages, which is probably why I had a hard time connecting to the bird stuff (well, that and the fact that it was bird people flying through the damn sky on big old ships). And I don't know if this was an intended outcome, but as the book wore on, I felt pretty sure that I was being given an environmental lecture? I could be completely off base here, but that's how some things came off.<br /></p><p><strong>Bottom Line:</strong> This was just not for me, but a lot of people absolutely adored it. There's apparently a sequel, but I don't think I will be partaking. I was fine with how this one ended, and honestly, I can't do anymore bird people.<br /><a href="http://itstartsatmidnight.com/2015/04/review-magonia-by-maria-dahvana-headley/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">This review was originally posted on It Starts at Midnight</a></p></span>
  <a data-text-id="16248912027448805930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
