<div id="review_1673940048" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1673940048" />
    <a title="Elise (On The Bookshelves)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51163760-elise-on-the-bookshelves"><img alt="Elise (On The Bookshelves)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578802562p2/51163760.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1673940048?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elise (On The Bookshelves)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elise (On The Bookshelves)" href="/user/show/51163760-elise-on-the-bookshelves">Elise (On The Bookshelves)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062391674" href="/book/show/23215491-magonia">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1673940048" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12186426672218379742"><a href='http://www.onthebookshelves.net/#!Recently-Read-Magonia-by-Maria-Dahvana-Headley/d97xh/5770da5c0cf2bcae6e403e1f' rel='nofollow noopener'>Link To On The Bookshelves Blog Post</a><br/><br/><b>“Yes, I’m a reader. Kill me. I could tell you I was raised in the library and the books were my only friends, but I didn’t do that, did I? Because I have mercy. I’m neither a genius nor a kid destined to become a wizard. I’m just me. I read stuff. Books are not my only friends, but we’re friendly. So there.”</b><br/><br/>RATING: 2/5 STARS<br/><br/>Since she was born, Aza Ray has struggled to breathe, talk and even just live thanks to her mysterious lung disease. One day she spots a s</span>
  <span id="freeText12186426672218379742" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.onthebookshelves.net/#!Recently-Read-Magonia-by-Maria-Dahvana-Headley/d97xh/5770da5c0cf2bcae6e403e1f" rel="nofollow noopener">Link To On The Bookshelves Blog Post</a><br /><br /><b>“Yes, I’m a reader. Kill me. I could tell you I was raised in the library and the books were my only friends, but I didn’t do that, did I? Because I have mercy. I’m neither a genius nor a kid destined to become a wizard. I’m just me. I read stuff. Books are not my only friends, but we’re friendly. So there.”</b><br /><br />RATING: 2/5 STARS<br /><br />Since she was born, Aza Ray has struggled to breathe, talk and even just live thanks to her mysterious lung disease. One day she spots a ship sailing in the sky, and this changes her life forever. When Aza is taken up there to the place they call Magonia, she feels normal, but why? Will Aza choose to stay in Magonia, or with the people she loves back down on earth?<br /><br />First of all, this book has a beautiful cover, but as they say, looks can be deceiving! This book is very bizarre. When you're not entirely sure how to put your thoughts into words, you know something just isn't right. A few moments were decent, but the majority were utterly confusing. It is such a strange concept overall. Yes, the idea of a world in the sky and ships sailing through the clouds is intriguing, a little reminiscent of the ship scene in the movie Stardust.<br /><br />Before we head to Magonia, we have the 'just BFF's but don't realise we love each other yet' romance between Aza and Jason. Jason is nerdy/cute, but Aza just falls flat throughout most of the story. It might have to do with the language used and the text formatting in some areas, there just felt like a lack of connection between the reader and protagonist. Oh, and as usual, there seems to be one of those potential love triangles.<br /><br />Next is Magonia - where the bird-like humans can have birds live inside their chests and then the bird-like humans who can fully turn into birds. Confusing? Yes, it really was. Aza ends up being a lost child of Magonia and can have a bird live inside her chest. The bird helps them to sing and gives them powers, and for Aza, hers are naturally the most powerful they've ever seen.<br /><br />Headley's writing is very whimsical and at some moments it was nice, but the overall confusion throughout the book utterly decimated the style.<br /><br />Overall, I would say make your own mind up about the book as it seems as though some people loved it? I'm not completely complaining because this book only cost me $3, but perhaps if I paid for a full priced book I would be crying. A short review because I didn't feel like there was much to say except it was eh and had the effect to cause you to start skim reading.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12186426672218379742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1227732909" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1227732909" />
    <a title="Lindsay Cummings" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4729981-lindsay-cummings"><img alt="Lindsay Cummings" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442622890p2/4729981.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1227732909?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay Cummings" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay Cummings" href="/user/show/4729981-lindsay-cummings">Lindsay Cummings</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1227732909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16202411345128580181">What a fantastic, beautifully written book. MAGONIA is unlike anything else. Wholly original, heartbreaking, exciting and intense, MAGONIA is one of the coolest books I've read in years.<br/><br/>The story begins with Aza Ray, a girl who, much like Hazel from THE FAULT IN OUR STARS, struggles to breathe. But Aza doesn't have cancer. She has an incredibly rare disease, and doctors are baffled by her. Aza doesn't ever feel quite right in the world--and things fast-forward, when she sees a real ship, sailing</span>
  <span id="freeText16202411345128580181" style="display:none">What a fantastic, beautifully written book. MAGONIA is unlike anything else. Wholly original, heartbreaking, exciting and intense, MAGONIA is one of the coolest books I've read in years.<br /><br />The story begins with Aza Ray, a girl who, much like Hazel from THE FAULT IN OUR STARS, struggles to breathe. But Aza doesn't have cancer. She has an incredibly rare disease, and doctors are baffled by her. Aza doesn't ever feel quite right in the world--and things fast-forward, when she sees a real ship, sailing through the sky.<br /><br />Aza's family chalks it up to a hallucination. But Aza's best friend, Jason, believes that what she saw truly could be real. When Aza dies, it seems like it's the end. <br /><br />Until she wakes up in another world. Or, rather (SPOILER) a world in the clouds. <br /><br />Enter the strangeness of this story. Enter the beauty. Enter the Peter-Pan-Esque-ness of MAGONIA. The world in the clouds truly does exist, and it's full of massive ships whose sailers are covered in feathers. Bird-people and Blue people make up the two races in MAGONIA. Their mission? Sail the skies, creating storms and natural distasters with their magical songs, and in turn, stay hidden while they sail down and steal crops from the human beings on the surface earth.<br /><br />Aza, apparently, has been to MAGONIA before, though she has no recollection of it. And while her family below on earth thinks she's dead...Jason, Aza's friend, is determined to find her.<br /><br />Trouble ensues, when Aza tries to decide which world she is most loyal to, where she truly belongs, and of course, there's danger. There's secrets. There's betrayal. There's love.<br /><br />This book...this book is beautiful. It's wacky, and it's told almost in a poetic, "What-does-this-sentence-even-mean-oh-I-get-it-now" style. Many will love it. Many will be baffled. Whether people devour it, or put it aside, EVERYONE will be talking about MAGONIA. And that's the coolest thing about this story.<br /><br />I'm on the "In love" side. And I hope that everyone who has a taste for adventure, fantasy, and worlds-apart romance will pick this one up.<br /><br />I'm dying for it to be a series. PLEASE, Maria Dahvana Headley. I need more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16202411345128580181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1466880189" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1466880189" />
    <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader"><img alt="Heidi The Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593309467p2/7986781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1466880189?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fantasy-and-sci-fi">fantasy-and-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1466880189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18245588614075502791">Aza Ray Boyle can't breathe. It seems like she has always been sick- inexplicably short of breath and weak.<br/><br/>This continuous illness has made her always feel different from the people around her. But, perhaps, there are stranger and more exotic reasons why she is different. Ones that Aza can't even imagine...<br/><br/>Jason is Aza's dearest friend. They are so close that they almost speak their own language.<br/><br/>He realizes there is more to Aza than meets the eye. How will Jason handle it when he discovers the s</span>
  <span id="freeText18245588614075502791" style="display:none">Aza Ray Boyle can't breathe. It seems like she has always been sick- inexplicably short of breath and weak.<br /><br />This continuous illness has made her always feel different from the people around her. But, perhaps, there are stranger and more exotic reasons why she is different. Ones that Aza can't even imagine...<br /><br />Jason is Aza's dearest friend. They are so close that they almost speak their own language.<br /><br />He realizes there is more to Aza than meets the eye. How will Jason handle it when he discovers the shocking truth?<br /><br />This young adult fantasy is weird, but I enjoyed it.<br /><br />That's probably because I read a lot of weird, non-fiction. The story of Magonia, a world in the sky above the every day world which we know, has shown up in some of those books.<br /><br />One of those books, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/406344.Passport_to_Magonia_On_UFOs__Folklore__and_Parallel_Worlds" title="Passport to Magonia On UFOs, Folklore, and Parallel Worlds by Jacques F. Vallée" rel="nofollow noopener">Passport to Magonia: On UFOs, Folklore, and Parallel Worlds</a>, captured my imagination.<br /><br />That book recounts an incident where a bunch of villagers were holding church service and they heard a crash outside. They went to investigate the noise and discovered what appeared to be a ship anchor attached to the roof of their church. It was connected to, this just blows my mind, a ship in the sky. This supposedly happened in 1211 AD.<br /><br />The astonishing thing about <i>Passport to Magonia</i> is it has pages and pages of stories like that, eyewitness accounts of bizarre ships, people, and incidents concerning people from the sky. And they all actually happened, reportedly.<br /><br />I remember thinking that an author needed to get her hands on these stories and turn it into something fantastic. Maria Dahvana Headley used a different source material than the book that I read, but does a good job bringing a mysterious blip in history to life.<br /><br />She has the ability to interweave actual events with fantasy fiction story lines so that the two begin to blur in the reader's mind.<br /><br />I read Headley's first book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9684527.Queen_of_Kings" title="Queen of Kings by Maria Dahvana Headley" rel="nofollow noopener">Queen of Kings</a> years ago and I remember being struck by its originality.<br /><br />Headley took Cleopatra's life and turned it into a vampire story. It sounds sort of silly described that way, (oh, ANOTHER vampire story) but it is actually rather fun.<br /><br />I had read Margaret George's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10115.The_Memoirs_of_Cleopatra" title="The Memoirs of Cleopatra by Margaret George" rel="nofollow noopener">The Memoirs of Cleopatra</a> shortly before <i>Queen of Kings</i> so I had a pretty good idea of the actual story of the Egyptian queen.<br /><br />Back to this book, <i>Magonia</i> isn't going to appeal to everyone.<br /><br />I was, at first, rather turned off by the uber-intellectual back and forth conversations of the main characters- Jason and Aza.<br /><br />I think, since the mega success of John Green's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a>, authors make their teenage protagonists so brainy and well-spoken, it is just unbelievable.<br /><br />I mean, it's been awhile, but I remember high school. My peers and I were lucky if we could string two cogent sentences together, let alone present verbal dissertations on the meaning of pi.<br /><br />Anyway, once I was able to look past their flowery repartee, I got really into the story.<br /><br />Headley paints a magical and dangerous world.<br /><br />If you enjoyed <i>Magonia</i>, you may also enjoy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22833921.The_Mermaid_s_Sister" title="The Mermaid's Sister by Carrie Anne Noble" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mermaid's Sister</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17817631.Under_the_Empyrean_Sky__The_Heartland_Trilogy___1_" title="Under the Empyrean Sky (The Heartland Trilogy, #1) by Chuck Wendig" rel="nofollow noopener">Under the Empyrean Sky</a>. Both are young adult novels and take place in fantasy worlds that are so close to the world we know, but different in surprising ways.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18245588614075502791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2819298733168934208">I am lost of words to describe how magical, astonishing, beautiful and original this book was. I mean, I can say Magonia is beautiful but it is more than that. It is like all my favorite things are in one place and I am glued to the ground, seeing and feeling them. It's like I am releasing bright lights that made me glowing.<br/><br/>The first time I saw that cover, I knew in myself that a great reading experience is coming on my way. And I wasn't wrong. Magonia may not be a perfect book but it took me to</span>
  <span id="freeText2819298733168934208" style="display:none">I am lost of words to describe how magical, astonishing, beautiful and original this book was. I mean, I can say Magonia is beautiful but it is more than that. It is like all my favorite things are in one place and I am glued to the ground, seeing and feeling them. It's like I am releasing bright lights that made me glowing.<br /><br />The first time I saw that cover, I knew in myself that a great reading experience is coming on my way. And I wasn't wrong. Magonia may not be a perfect book but it took me to a wonderful place, a wonderful journey. And for me it is one of the books that gave me the feeling how fun, enjoyable and euphoric reading is.</span>

<div id="review_1248113915" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1248113915" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1248113915?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1248113915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9353823449173653031">Oh, Magonia, you strange, strange book, it’s going to take me months to decipher you. <br/><br/>Magonia by Maria Dahvana Headley has so many things going for it, I’m not even sure where to begin. It’s a book that simply refuses to be compared or classified; even determining its genre is proving to be impossible. It’s a delightful combination of science fiction, fantasy, and even dystopia, and it easily balances the three, never allowing one to overtake the others.<br/><br/>Headley brings us a previously unexplored </span>
  <span id="freeText9353823449173653031" style="display:none">Oh, Magonia, you strange, strange book, it’s going to take me months to decipher you. <br><br>Magonia by Maria Dahvana Headley has so many things going for it, I’m not even sure where to begin. It’s a book that simply refuses to be compared or classified; even determining its genre is proving to be impossible. It’s a delightful combination of science fiction, fantasy, and even dystopia, and it easily balances the three, never allowing one to overtake the others.<br><br>Headley brings us a previously unexplored story of flying ships and sky sailors. She took a fairly unknown story from the 9th century, used it to her best advantage, and breathed something wholly new and original into it for good measure. The final result is magical: a cloud realm, bird people, sky pirates and magical songs, all combined to create a book unlike anything I’ve ever read before. <br><br>Headley writing style is lyrical and gorgeous. There have been many comparisons to Laini Taylor and Neil Gaiman, and they aren’t entirely exaggerated or wrong. But I must say that in this too, she gives us something that’s entirely her own. Her understanding and use of language to create or dispel tension, to project moods and atmosphere, is simply astonishing. <br><br>The story is told from two points of view, and both Aza and Jason are amazing characters. Intelligent, resourceful, geeky, unusual, and loyal, they’ve depended on each other for pretty much everything since they were five years old. When they get separated, Jason’s point of view becomes more than just welcome – it becomes necessary to understand his part of the story, but it also strengthens the emotional tension and offers us an insight into his peculiar and understanding nature.<br><br> There were times when Aza’s second world became a bit overwhelming. Although it doesn’t seem that way, probably thanks to Headley’s unusual writing style, the pacing is pretty fast and it sometimes doesn’t give us enough time to process. I’m usually in favor of losing extra chapters and paragraphs, but this book would have benefited from an extra fifty or hundred pages. With such a marvelous worldbuilding, Headley should have allowed herself to use it to its full potential, which I don’t think she’s done. <br><br>The ending of Magonia is very satisfactory, but there is much room for a sequel. There hasn’t been an announcement so far, at least I wasn’t able to find one, but I sincerely hope that there’s a second book in the works because this world has so much more to give. <br><br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText2733100876377395604" style="display:none">An Electronic Advanced Reader Copy was provided by the publisher via Edelweiss for review.<br /><br />DNF'd at 47%.. Highly creative with magical flying ships and bird people who sing their way through chores, I thought Magonia had all the bare bones for a great novel, but I just didn't care about the characters as I would have liked. They would ramble way too much to the point where my eyes would glaze over. I'm guessing this is supposed to be relevant but I just grew bored with their rambles. Not only does Aza the main character ramble, but Jason her best friend and the other point of view did too. Not to say I don't respect the quirky imaginations of these two characters, I'm just saying they weren't for me. I'm sure the story would have picked up and I'm sure there's a lot more to be said within Aza's new journey (especially with apparently sexy Dai) but I found it to be too weird for me.</span>

<div id="review_1109637921" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1109637921" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1109637921?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23621681-magonia">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=epic-reads-for-light-and-dark-pup">epic-reads-for-light-and-dark-pup</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=my-favorite-covers">my-favorite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1109637921" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15280533167263904478"><br/><b>
  <i>"You hold no horrors for me."</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/>I'm not guna lie....this book is weird. <i>Beyond</i> weird. And it is what I would normally say was 'too out there, for me.' But, once again, a little birdie told me how amazing it was and hell, here I am again adding another favorite to my list. I think it's safe to say that no amount of weirdness could have quelled my instant, butterfly-induced reaction to Jason and Aza's heartbreaking friendship from the very beginning of this story. <b>It was instantaneous, the viscer</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15280533167263904478" style="display:none"><br><b>
  <i>"You hold no horrors for me."</i>
</b><br><br><br>I'm not guna lie....this book is weird. <i>Beyond</i> weird. And it is what I would normally say was 'too out there, for me.' But, once again, a little birdie told me how amazing it was and hell, here I am again adding another favorite to my list. I think it's safe to say that no amount of weirdness could have quelled my instant, butterfly-induced reaction to Jason and Aza's heartbreaking friendship from the very beginning of this story. <b>It was instantaneous, the visceral reaction I had to this guy</b>, and very rarely do I fall so hard, so quick, for a dude. I mean, come on, they generally have to work a <i>little</i> bit for my affections. But, <b>this book, breaking all of my carefully placed rules and guidelines, broke the barrier and became an instant-I need to re-read this immediately story</b>, and, for that, I will never forget it.<br><br><br><br><b>I never thought this would happen. <br>I thought this would probably happen. <br>I knew this was coming. <br>I didn't see this coming.</b><br>-Jason<br><br><br>While I don't feel like I should say much, seeing as I don't really know what all people are supposed to know, I have to comment on the two main characters and the attachment they have to one another. Being an outsider, Aza didn't have many friends growing up. She has a rare disease they can't even put a name to because no one else has it. Well, okay then. So, one day when little boy Jason meets little girl Aza, he knows he MUST meet her, despite being a bitey, mean specimen of a girl. I think it was this moment (Eh, okay, I loved him before but...) when I truly knew how much I loved Jason and Aza's relationship. He knew he had to know her, and what followed after are years of amazing and adorable friendship. They speak in their own special way (as friends tend to do) and don't care what anyone thinks of them, and it was beautiful to see the support he gave her. And omg-<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[His note to her. I { } you more than ((([ ])))) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The way they just <i>know</i>...God I love it.<br><br><br><b>I feel bitey. He should believe me. He's the person who always believes me. I count on him to be my primary enabler of Vivid Imagination.</b><br><br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_msjpm0U4Yz1sfdd54o1_500_zps8n8obimv.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431957395ra/14886590.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_msjpm0U4Yz1sfdd54o1_500_zps8n8obimv.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br>Another thing I absolutely adored was Aza's unique voice. Being inside her head was just so funny. Every minute had me laughing or smiling because, I'll say it, <b>she's abrupt and rude and, frankly, a bitch.</b> But I loved this. She had so much snark and such a funny way of talking about her condition that it really just spoke to me and made it impossible for me to put the book down. One minute I was obsessed with Jason, but when he wasn't around, I adored her voice, as well. This was just such a fun and different read, and I cannot wait to re-read this story again, in spite of the weirdness that ensued in the middle. <br><br><br><b>Bang, bang, you're dead. Close your eyes and go to bed.</b><br><br><br>And that's another thing. Right when I got to the middle, I lost all of my reading time. It was dreadful, and it horribly effected the story-Reading 10% at a time, with such a short book, is terribly distracting. And this is a lot of the reason why I MUST read this again soon. Too many wonderful (and not so wonderful) things happened that I felt betrayed by my own lack of time because I couldn't give the story my full focus...this is one of my pet peeves, but, for once, I really mean it and will fulfill my statement when I say that I will be <b>reading this again very, very soon.</b> <br><br><br><br><b>I know that's trite. Yes, I'm a reader. Kill me. I could tell you I was raised in the library and the books were my only friends, but I didn't do that, did I? Because I have mercy. I'm neither a genius nor a kid destined to become a wizard. I'm just me. I read stuff. Books are not my only friends, but we're friendly. So there.</b><br><br><br>So, yeah, I could go on and on and on about wild and weird things, but it would defeat the purpose of what I'm trying to do here-create an heir of mystery. <b>Now, if you don't like to stray into fantasy very much, I really wouldn't read this story.</b> While Jason and Aza's relationship and the things that happened were enough to counteract the weird, for me, it might not be the same for you. Because...Birds. Yeah. So. Make a wise decision when you pick this one up. Nothing aggravates me more than someone saying they hated a book they damn well knew was going to be different-These people have only themselves to blame-plenty of people said this was odd, and you have been warned thusly. <br><br><br><br><b>No one asked ME when the lab published a paper in <i>Nature</i> and gave this disease my name. I would've said no. I'd like to have named my disease myself: the Jackass, or maybe something ugly, such as Elmer or Clive.</b><br><br><br><br>Now, I don't know how I can so easily skirt around a subject and talk about a whole lot of nothing, but I sure as hell did it. So, pick this one up, don't pick it up, just know, the writing is fresh and fun and the story is funny while being incredibly bizarre and a little bit heart-breaking. In a word?? It was <b>wonderful.</b><br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/%20" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="60" width="139" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409285880i/10960212.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>

<div id="review_1229001127" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1229001127" />
    <a title="Taylor Knight" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12627819-taylor-knight"><img alt="Taylor Knight" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536879168p2/12627819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1229001127?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taylor Knight" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taylor Knight" href="/user/show/12627819-taylor-knight">Taylor Knight</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12627819-taylor-knight?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1229001127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9292420390633498756"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437335915ra/15573372.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I was so excited to read this book. The concept sounded so good and I knew I needed this book in my life. I was so excited and pumped, I didn't stop to think that I might not like this book as much as I thought I would. I should have calmed down before starting this book because after 50 pages, I felt like I would drown in my disappointment. <br/><br/>Right away, the tone of this book caught me off guard. The main character was so snarky and I was not expecting that. At first, I was really on board with A</span>
  <span id="freeText9292420390633498756" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437335915ra/15573372.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I was so excited to read this book. The concept sounded so good and I knew I needed this book in my life. I was so excited and pumped, I didn't stop to think that I might not like this book as much as I thought I would. I should have calmed down before starting this book because after 50 pages, I felt like I would drown in my disappointment. <br><br>Right away, the tone of this book caught me off guard. The main character was so snarky and I was not expecting that. At first, I was really on board with Aza and her attitude but after 40 pages, I couldn't take it much more. There's a fine line between good snarky attitude and just being a brat. I felt like Aza was just a brat. I wanted to tell her to just chill out for a second. I think the hardest part is I wouldn't be friends with Aza if she was real. I think that's a really important quality for characters to have. If I can't relate to the main character (which I didn't with Aza) then I want to be able to feel like we would be friends. I didn't feel any of that with Aza. Granted, I did think she got better though out the book but the damage was already done.<br><br>I did really like the writing though. It was really well written. <br>I could go on and on about how much I love the concept of this book. It's so unlike anything I've read before and that aspect of the blew my mind. <br><br>Overall, I liked everything about this book except the main character. I just couldn't relate to her or connect to her. I feel like it's more of a personal opinion than something actually "wrong" with the book. I'm definitely going to be rereading this book (because I'm determined to love it) but as of right now, I'm not really digging it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9292420390633498756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1084721722" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1084721722" />
    <a title="gio" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23204207-gio"><img alt="gio" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597613414p2/23204207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1084721722?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="gio" class="user" itemprop="url" name="gio" href="/user/show/23204207-gio">gio</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1084721722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17645071430996684745"><br/>4.25 (I've just discovered that there's a sequel, so now that open ending makes sense. Hopefully.)<br/><br/><b>“Life and death aren’t as different from each other as I thought they were. This isn’t like walking into a new country. This is like walking into a new room in the same house. This is like sharing a hallway and the same row of framed family pictures, but there’s a glass wall between.”</b><br/><br/>Well, this one was weird. I guess it's why it was blurbed by Neil Gaiman. Magonia does have the feeling that some of </span>
  <span id="freeText17645071430996684745" style="display:none"><br />4.25 (I've just discovered that there's a sequel, so now that open ending makes sense. Hopefully.)<br /><br /><b>“Life and death aren’t as different from each other as I thought they were. This isn’t like walking into a new country. This is like walking into a new room in the same house. This is like sharing a hallway and the same row of framed family pictures, but there’s a glass wall between.”</b><br /><br />Well, this one was weird. I guess it's why it was blurbed by Neil Gaiman. Magonia does have the feeling that some of his book have, like you have stumbled upon something so unique and so strange that you can't understand everything about it. Sometimes it was too strange, like the author had too many ideas for such a short book, but overall it worked. <br /><br />Aza can't breathe. She has been diagnosed with a mysterious lung disease and the longer she lives the harder it is for her to breathe. She knows that she doesn't have much more days to live and as the time passes she starts seeing things. Up in the sky. Ships. Her family says it's because of her medication, and only her friend, Jason, believes that there might be something more. However it seems that Aza's time has come and that she is truly lost to our world. But just when the darkness welcomes her she finds out that as lost as she is to our world she might have found another. Magonia, a land of trading ships up in the sky. There she isn't frail, or weak, or ill. In Magonia Aza is a powerful person. A leader, a new hope for her people. But can she forget the people she left behind?<br /><br />See, this book is crazy. Like, literally crazy. There are flying ships, flying whales and even people with tiny birds inside of them. And these strange elements fit into the story. Incredibly so, but they do. And I couldn't help but appreciate the author's imagination and ideas, because they are new in a sea of already seen books. The world-building and this kind of magic system are well written and I wish they would have entered the story sooner, because they were so interesting. <br /><br />If I had to find some flaws I'd say that the ending was really rushed, which is something I didn't like much, and that...sometimes the book did become too strange. There are things you can't "accept", and it's like your mind refuses to actually understand. <br /><br />So...strange. Unique, a little bit mad but magical. If you're not up to some crazy things then Magonia is not your book. But if you want to read something you have never seen before I suggest you try it out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17645071430996684745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1117049703" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1117049703" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1117049703?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=better-than-i-expected">better-than-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=multi-povs">multi-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=tough-subjects">tough-subjects</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1117049703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13424736434270529368">Quick review for a quick read. Dude, I didn't know what I was getting myself into when I picked up Maria Dahvana Headley's "Magonia". Suffice to say, I'm quite impressed by it. I really didn't expect it to be this emotionally invested, intense, and imaginative read. Totally ended up enjoying the journey it took me on and it's one of those stories that will stick out in my mind for a long time to come. I mean, the closest of a comparison that I can make of "Magonia" to anything I've seen or read </span>
  <span id="freeText13424736434270529368" style="display:none">Quick review for a quick read. Dude, I didn't know what I was getting myself into when I picked up Maria Dahvana Headley's "Magonia". Suffice to say, I'm quite impressed by it. I really didn't expect it to be this emotionally invested, intense, and imaginative read. Totally ended up enjoying the journey it took me on and it's one of those stories that will stick out in my mind for a long time to come. I mean, the closest of a comparison that I can make of "Magonia" to anything I've seen or read is the anime/manga series Rahxephon, but that's notably because of the power of the protagonists with song/singing and their "special" roles/identities in their societies, but even then, it's not that close. It takes on a very different mythos than what is commonly found in YA fantasy. (And thank goodness for that, because it's a breath of fresh air creativity wise. Why can't more YA books be like this?!)<br /><br />There were moments where I really connected with the emotional intensity of Aza's experiences. From her lifelong battle of unexplained illness to being separated from those she loves in what seems like a permanent capacity. Also finding herself in a completely different identity and realm with choices she has to make in terms of the role she plays and the loyalties she shows. There are some caveats to it though, where the emotion has moments when it feels like it overpresses the point a bit too much for the given context, but I could say that I could palpate it and see why Aza reacts the way she does. Her voice is genuine, if a bit rocky to start before it starts smoothing out over the course of events in the novel. Jason was a nice alternate perspective, and I'm glad this book never hit the insta-love button or made the romance feel so out of place that it took over the story. I'm definitely very happy to see a YA fantasy that prominently focuses on the otherworldly elements, the action, the overarching conflict and relationships and takes the mythos and turns it into something that has the chance to shine on its own and prominently in the story. Though, if I could give a critique of it - there are certain aspects of the world depiction that seemed to me like they skimmed the surface and didn't quite immerse me as much as I hoped it would. I think I understood the world of Magonia and the skyships and rituals/beliefs that were depicted to a degree here, but there were details that still felt like they needed fleshing out.<br /><br />I honestly can't take away from what was offered here, though. I didn't want to put this book down when I picked it up and found myself marathoning at a breakneck pace through the audiobook (brilliantly narrated by Therese Plummer and Michael Crouch. Plummer might get a nod for my favorite female narration this year because her depiction of Aza was spot on.) I know that I want to read more in this world and feel like I'm invested in the characters and their journeys to see where they go from here - so I'm definitely on board for the next book in this series.<br /><br />Overall score: 4/5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="13424736434270529368" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1688909404" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1688909404" />
    <a title="Joanna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17348951-joanna"><img alt="Joanna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475418532p2/17348951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1688909404?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanna " href="/user/show/17348951-joanna">Joanna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1688909404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6729844735313362333"><b> Updated review and star rating March 3 2017. Dropped rating from 2 stars to 1 star. </b><br/><br/>This book took me an incredibly long time to read and it was painful to do so as well. I pretty much made myself finish this book even though I seriously considered putting it in my DNF pile. <br/><br/>Honestly the most moving part of the whole book was from page 305-309. Really very beautiful and touching. Otherwise this book was just a jumble. I didn't like any of the characters. The MC was always awkward and left in th</span>
  <span id="freeText6729844735313362333" style="display:none"><b> Updated review and star rating March 3 2017. Dropped rating from 2 stars to 1 star. </b><br /><br />This book took me an incredibly long time to read and it was painful to do so as well. I pretty much made myself finish this book even though I seriously considered putting it in my DNF pile. <br /><br />Honestly the most moving part of the whole book was from page 305-309. Really very beautiful and touching. Otherwise this book was just a jumble. I didn't like any of the characters. The MC was always awkward and left in the dark about a lot of issues. Her male best friend was a bit obsessive and moody which I could partially understand due to the situation but still it left a sour note in my mouth. Aside from the lack lustre characters the writing and world building were not that great. Even after finishing the book, I am still unsure of the reason why the main character was on Earth in the first place. There is just so much inconsistency in the plot and the world building and it's dressed up in overly flowery language. I mean what was the point?<br /><br />I really dislike when a book aims to be pretentious. It's a real turn off and so I'm not going to continue with this series. Thank goodness I only borrowed this from the library cause I was going to buy it for the cover. A lesson learned for me and for all of us easily swayed by a beautiful book cover. Sometimes not everything that shines is gold. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6729844735313362333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1269161347" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1269161347" />
    <a title="Kathe L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25921490-kathe-l"><img alt="Kathe L" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421550107p2/25921490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1269161347?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathe L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathe L" href="/user/show/25921490-kathe-l">Kathe L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=didn-t-expect-to-be-so-good">didn-t-expect-to-be-so-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=fav-female-characters">fav-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=cute-boy-you-made-me-swoon">cute-boy-you-made-me-swoon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1269161347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3643297378685421282"><b>4,5 stars, maybe?</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380386972ra/746711.gif' width='350' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is <i>so</i> hard to write. You know those days when you just read? I read, easily, 4 hours straight plus all the other hours that I wasn't eating today. Because this book, oh man. This book demands your full attention and your full time. It's a book that starts in an unpredictable way and turns your world upside down. <br/><br/><b>"In some on the old stories (...), the patterns of the stars form letters. Celestial alphabets. Writing that gets rewritten as the earth moves. If you look at the s</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3643297378685421282" style="display:none"><b>4,5 stars, maybe?</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380386972ra/746711.gif" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is <i>so</i> hard to write. You know those days when you just read? I read, easily, 4 hours straight plus all the other hours that I wasn't eating today. Because this book, oh man. This book demands your full attention and your full time. It's a book that starts in an unpredictable way and turns your world upside down. <br><br><b>"In some on the old stories (...), the patterns of the stars form letters. Celestial alphabets. Writing that gets rewritten as the earth moves. If you look at the sky that way, it's this massive shifting poem, or maybe a letter, first written by one author, and then, when the earth moves, annotated by another. So I stare and stare until, one day, I can read it."</b><br><br>This quote, this writing, the sequel of things that happen. I won't say what this is about. The first thing I thought was: "what a weird book." But this is as good as weird goes. It's weird because it was something new to me, because it was unpredictable and because it took me some time to get used to it, but then, when I did, I was reading each word with hurry and fear and attention. <br><br><i>"People actually, amazingly, think we're normal teenagers in love."</i><br><br><i>The characters?</i> There's Aza and Jason, and they completely owned my heart. <s>This year is bringing me a lot of book boyfriends.</s> I thought after Jazz I wouldn't be amazed at another character, but no. Jason was a boy who made me suffer alongside him. And he was just so cute and perfect, he owned me from the very first scene with Aza. And Aza? She was just so incredibly different from every character I've ever read about! She is fierce, loving, brave. She has a way with words that makes her unique. She has a caring heart, most important of all. And to have this book in both POV's? Usually, I have a favorite POV but these two point of views were so important to the story that I got excited over any of them. Why did I finish this so quickly, you can guess. <s>The first POV from Jason completely broke my heart, though.</s> <br><br><b>-&gt;</b> I hated some character with all my being, though. <br><b>-&gt;</b> There's sort of a love triangle that isn't quite a threat, but it's confusing. <br><b>-&gt;</b> This book will make you miss something when you finish it. <br><b>-&gt;</b> It is full of new discoveries.<br><b>-&gt;</b> Magonia ruined me for other fantasy books. <br><br><i>What a strange name is Magonia</i>, I thought yesterday when I picked this up. And is it fantasy? Is it romance? Is a combination of both, but a book that it's unlike everything you've ever read. This book is the type of book that could have been a complete win for me or a complete disaster. It's about magic, family, morals. Friendship, love. How can I read other fantasy books after this? It will be very, very hard. Surely, this is one of the books that surprised me the most this year because I didn't expect it to be this great. Maybe it is the magic of it, though. <br><br><b>"There was no way I could live another moment without Aza Ray knowing my name."</b><br><br><s>Jason, Jason, Jason, be still my heart &lt;3</s> Fantasy fans out there, try this one. It's different, unique, weird, <b>charming.</b> Charming is definitely the best word to describe it. All in all, I couldn't be happier I spent my afternoon with this book. And that's the best feeling, right? </span>
  <a data-text-id="3643297378685421282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1090713590" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1090713590" />
    <a title="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5383215-nereyda-nick-nereyda-s-infinite-booklist"><img alt="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445582024p2/5383215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1090713590?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)" href="/user/show/5383215-nereyda-nick-nereyda-s-infinite-booklist">Nereyda (Nick &amp; Nereyda&#39;s Infinite Booklist)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1090713590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6895548672014358580">I know this book was a little bit too weird for some people, but I was odly fascinated by it. What made this even better for me was how amazing the audio performance was for this one. This kind of book is not my usual read, and I was a little bit scared off by the reviews at first. But once I found out that Michael Crouch was narrating this one, I knew I had to listen to it! Listening to the book felt a bit like hearing a movie and I ended up breezing through this one in a few hours.<br/><br/>Magonia was </span>
  <span id="freeText6895548672014358580" style="display:none">I know this book was a little bit too weird for some people, but I was odly fascinated by it. What made this even better for me was how amazing the audio performance was for this one. This kind of book is not my usual read, and I was a little bit scared off by the reviews at first. But once I found out that Michael Crouch was narrating this one, I knew I had to listen to it! Listening to the book felt a bit like hearing a movie and I ended up breezing through this one in a few hours.<br><br>Magonia was such a unique story, and I’m not exactly sure what it is yet. It felt a bit like sci-fi and a bit of everything else. Aza has always struggled just to even breathe on Earth. With a mysterious lung disease that makes it hard to breath and speak, she’s always felt like she doesn’t belong. Even if her family and her best friend Jason do everything to make her feel like she does. Jason, who has feelings for Aza (it’s mutual), is the only one who believes Aza when she tells him about the ships she sees in the skies. But right as they both decide to finally make their move, Aza is taken to Magonia where she is told is where she belongs. Everyone believes Aza is dead, except for Jason, who is determined to do whatever he can to find her, and save her.<br><br>There is no doubt that Magonia was a strange kind of read, but I couldn’t help but like it more because of it. My favorite part of the story was the best friends-romance between Aza and Jason. I loved that we were able to get his POV chapters, not just because I really liked Michael Crouch as narrator, but because his scenes were my favorite. I loved how he was so desperate to save her then find once she was taken. His obsessiveness with numbers was adorable, as well as the reason behind it. Fingers crossed that this doesn’t develop a love triangle in the next book. Speaking of the next book, when I read this, there was no listing on Goodreads about there being a sequel. But with the way things ended, there had to be a sequel! I was hoping that there would be and I’m excited that they finally announced it. I’m looking forward to not only the next book, but the next audiobook. I hope the next book is as weirdly fascinating as this one, and that the same narrators come back. Oh, and I wouldn’t mind another gorgeous cover for the next book either. Don’t let the weirdness scare you away! Give this one a shot, preferably on audio.<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments:</b> I was hoping this one would be released on audio, because I wanted to read it, but I also struggle with having to actually read books like this. Audio is the way to go for me. When I found out Michael Crouch was one of the narrators, I immediately added this to my wish list. I first heard Micheal Crouch in Simon vs. The Homo Sapiens Agenda (which was awesome!) and even though I was a little bit worried I would keep hearing Simon this time around, I knew he could pull it off. And he did. Michael Crouch really has to do more YA books because he has a voice that is perfect for it. He doesn’t sound too old and he is a very talented narrator. I’ll be on the lookout for more books narrated by him. Therese Plummer was a new narrator for me, but she was so good. She complemented Crouch so well and was amazing in all of her scenes as Aza. The performance in this audio was so soooo good!<br><br><b>4 out of 5 stars</b><br><br><div>
  <div>
    <a target="_blank" href="http://www.polyvore.com/where_see_fashion_magonia/set?.embedder=8312598&amp;.svc=copypaste&amp;id=140997052" rel="nofollow noopener">

    </a>
  </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MrN1aQHdG7OaBZyEixpFB2b/AB+wRHjCxvgxV4HRyxR79vAdxXhEOYXs3cJp2B/XmN9qVeZY3oFjXU+W5wY7ow==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3I0sh8BLZuE296KXF31SU3ceICiRCotiDKafolZXHeWVyKnzBO45ayke49H1vwiDiT5KYscWLSGpA+FjMIDtUg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1643292771749055656">Maria Dahvana Headley is the New York Times-bestselling author of, most recently, THE MERE WIFE (out July 17, 2018 from MCD/FSG). Upcoming in 2019 is a new translation of BEOWULF, also from FSG. As well, she is the author of the young adult skyship novels MAGONIA and AERIE from HarperCollins, the dark fantasy/alt-history novel QUEEN OF KINGS, the internationally bestselling memoir THE YEAR OF YES,</span>
  <span id="freeText1643292771749055656" style="display:none">Maria Dahvana Headley is the New York Times-bestselling author of, most recently, THE MERE WIFE (out July 17, 2018 from MCD/FSG). Upcoming in 2019 is a new translation of BEOWULF, also from FSG. As well, she is the author of the young adult skyship novels MAGONIA and AERIE from HarperCollins, the dark fantasy/alt-history novel QUEEN OF KINGS, the internationally bestselling memoir THE YEAR OF YES, and THE END OF THE SENTENCE, a novella co-written with Kat Howard, from Subterranean. With Neil Gaiman, she is the New York Times-bestselling co-editor of the monster anthology UNNATURAL CREATURES, benefitting 826DC. <br /><br />Her Nebula,Shirley Jackson and World Fantasy award-nominated short fiction has appeared on Tor.com, and in The Toast, Clarkesworld, Lightspeed, Nightmare, Apex, The Journal of Unlikely Entomology, Subterranean Online, Glitter &amp; Mayhem and Jurassic London's The Lowest Heaven and The Book of the Dead, Uncanny, Shimmer, and more. It's anthologized in Best American Fantasy and Science Fiction, as well as the 2013 and 2014 editions of Rich Horton's The Year's Best Fantasy &amp; Science Fiction, &amp; Paula Guran's 2013 The Year's Best Dark Fantasy &amp; Horror, in The Year's Best Weird Volume 1, ed. Laird Barron, and in Wastelands, Vol 2, among others. She's also a playwright and essayist. <br /><br />She grew up in rural Idaho on a sled-dog ranch, spent part of her 20's as a pirate negotiator and ship marketer in the maritime industry, and now lives in Brooklyn in an apartment shared with a seven-foot-long stuffed crocodile. </span>
